OUT\\n30:         floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\\n31:         int n_threads):\\n32:     \\\"\\\"\\\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for dense input data.\\n33: \\n34:     Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\\n35:     centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\\n36:     The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\\n37:     and the closest center.\\n38: \\n39:     The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\\n40:     For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\\n41:     previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\\n42:     lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\\n43:     cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\\n44:     computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\\n45:     it is unlikely to be assigned to.\\n46: \\n47:     Parameters\\n48:     ----------\\n49:     X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\\n50:         The input data.\\n51: \\n52:     centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\\n53:         The cluster centers.\\n54: \\n55:     center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\\\\n56:             dtype=floating\\n57:         The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\\n58: \\n59:     labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\\n60:         The label for each sample. OUT\\n105:         floating[::1] upper_bounds,                    # OUT\\n106:         floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\\n107:         int n_threads):\\n108:     \\\"\\\"\\\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for sparse input data.\\n109: \\n110:     Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\\n111:     centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\\n112:     The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\\n113:     and the closest center.\\n114: \\n115:     The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\\n116:     For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\\n117:     previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\\n118:     lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\\n119:     cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. int[::1] labels,                               # INOUT\\n197:         floating[::1] center_shift,                    # OUT\\n198:         int n_threads,\\n199:         bint update_centers=True):\\n200:     \\\"\\\"\\\"Single iteration of K-means Elkan algorithm with dense input.\\n201: \\n202:     Update labels and centers (inplace), for one iteration, distributed\\n203:     over data chunks.\\n204: \\n205:     Parameters\\n206:     ----------\\n207:     X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\\n208:         The observations to cluster.\\n209: OUT\\n363:         bint update_centers) noexcept nogil:\\n364:     \\\"\\\"\\\"K-means combined EM step for one dense data chunk.\\n365: \\n366:     Compute the partial contribution of a single data chunk to the labels and\\n367:     centers.\\n368:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n369:     cdef:\\n370:         int n_samples = labels.shape[0]\\n371:         int n_clusters = centers_old.shape[0]\\n372:         int n_features = centers_old.shape[1]\\n373: \\n374:         floating upper_bound, distance\\n375:         int i, j, k, label\\n376: \\n377:     for i in range(n_samples):\\n378:         upper_bound = upper_bounds[i]\\n379:         bounds_tight = 0\\n380:         label = labels[i]\\n381: \\n382:         # OUT\\n30:         floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\\n31:         int n_threads):\\n32:     \\\"\\\"\\\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for dense input data.\\n33: \\n34:     Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\\n35:     centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\\n36:     The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\\n37:     and the closest center.\\n38: \\n39:     The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\\n40:     For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\\n41:     previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\\n42:     lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\\n43:     cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\\n44:     computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\\n45:     it is unlikely to be assigned to.\\n46: \\n47:     Parameters\\n48:     ----------\\n49:     X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\\n50:         The input data.\\n51: \\n52:     centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\\n53:         The cluster centers.\\n54: \\n55:     center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\\\\n56:             dtype=floating\\n57:         The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\\n58: \\n59:     labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\\n60:         The label for each sample. This array is modified in place.\\n65: \\n66:     lower_bounds : ndarray, of shape(n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\\n67:         The lower bound on the distance between each sample and each cluster\\n68:         center. Since both the lower bound and center-to-center distance provide estimates, if both suggest B is farther than A, the actual distance computation might be skippable. This suggests AND would be more appropriate than OR.\n\nHowever, changing OR to AND could compromise correctness—the current logic recomputes the upper bound when needed, then checks both conditions to decide whether to compute the distance to cluster j. Switching to AND might cause missed relabelings. The triangle inequality is the foundation here, so I should implement a straightforward optimization: skip clusters that are provably farther than the current upper bound using the center-to-center distances already available.\n\nI could also try reordering clusters by their distance to the current one to find closer matches faster, or batch distance calculations with NumPy, though sorting adds overhead. The code then computes the actual Euclidean distance if the bounds haven't been tightened yet.\n\nAfter tightening the upper bound, there's a second distance computation that uses an OR condition instead of AND. the\n    lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\n    cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\n    computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\n    it is unlikely to be assigned to.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The input data.\n\n    centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The cluster centers.\n\n    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n            dtype=floating\n        The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\n\n    labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\n        The label for each sample. This array is modified in place.\n\n    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples,), dtype=floating\n        The upper bound on the distance between each sample and its closest\n        cluster center. This array is modified in place.\n\n    lower_bounds : ndarray, of shape(n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\n        The lower bound on the distance between each sample and each cluster\n        center. This array is modified in place.\n\n    n_threads : int\n        The number of threads to be used by openmp.\n    \"\"\"\n    cdef:\n        int n_samples = X.shape[0]\n        int n_clusters = centers.shape[0]\n        int n_features = X.shape[1]\n\n        floating min_dist, dist\n        int best_cluster, i, j\n\n    for i in prange(\n        n_samples, num_threads=n_threads, schedule='static', nogil=True\n    ):\n        best_cluster = 0\n        min_dist = _euclidean_dense_dense(&X[i, 0], &centers[0, 0],\n                                          n_features, True)\n        lower_bounds[i, 0] = min_dist\n        for j in range(1, n_clusters):\n            if min_dist > center_half_distances[best_cluster, j]:\n                dist = _euclidean_dense_dense(&X[i, 0], &centers[j, 0],\n                                              n_features, True)\n                lower_bounds[i, j] = dist\n                if dist < min_dist:\n                    min_dist = dist\n                    best_cluster = j\n        labels[i] = best_cluster\n        upper_bounds[i] = min_dist\n\n\ndef init_bounds_sparse(\n        X,                                             # j\n\n        floating[::1] centers_squared_norms = row_norms(centers, squared=True)\n\n    for i in prange(\n        n_samples, num_threads=n_threads, schedule='static', nogil=True\n    ):\n int n_threads):\n    \"\"\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for dense input data.\n\n    Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\n    centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\n    The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\n    and the closest center.\n\n    The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\n    For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\n    previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\n    lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\n    cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\n    computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\n    it is unlikely to be assigned to.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The input data.\n\n    centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The cluster centers.\n\n    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n            dtype=floating\n        The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\n\n    labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\n        The label for each sample.        - If True, the labels and the new centers will be computed, i.e. runs\n          the E-step and the M-step of the algorithm.\n        - If False, only the labels will be computed, i.e runs the E-step of\n          the algorithm. This is useful especially when calling predict on a\n          fitted model.\n    \"\"\"\n    cdef:\n        int n_samples = X.shape[0]\n        int n_features = X.shape[1]\n        int n_clusters = centers_new.shape[0]\n\n    if n_samples == 0:\n        # An empty array was passed, do nothing and return early (before\n        # attempting to compute n_chunks). This can typically happen when\n        # calling the prediction function of a bisecting k-means model with a\n        # large fraction of outliers.\n        return\n\n    cdef:\n        # hard-coded number of samples per chunk. Splitting in chunks is\n        # necessary to get parallelism. Chunk size chosen to be same as lloyd's\n        int n_samples_chunk = CHUNK_SIZE if n_samples > CHUNK_SIZE else n_samples\n        int n_chunks = n_samples // n_samples_chunk\n        int n_samples_rem = n_samples % n_samples_chunk\n        int chunk_idx\n        int start, end\n\n        int i, j, k\n\n        floating *centers_new_chunk\n        floating *weight_in_clusters_chunk\n\n        omp_lock_t lock\n\n    # count remainder chunk in total number of chunks\n    n_chunks += n_samples != n_chunks * n_samples_chunk\n\n    # number of threads should not be bigger than number of chunks\n    n_threads = min(n_threads, n_chunks)\n\n    if update_centers:\n        memset(&centers_new[0, 0], 0, n_clusters * n_features * sizeof(floating))\n        memset(&weight_in_clusters[0], 0, n_clusters * sizeof(floating))\n        omp_init_lock(&lock)\n\n    with nogil, parallel(num_threads=n_threads):\n        # Next center is not far away from the currently assigned center.\n        # Sample might need to be assigned to another center.\n        if not distance_next_center[label] >= upper_bound:\n\n            for j in range(n_clusters):\n\n                # for dense input data.\n\n    Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\n    centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\n    The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\n    and the closest center.\n\n    The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\n    For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\n    previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\n    lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\n    cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\n    computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\n    it is unlikely to be assigned to.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The input data.\n\n    centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The cluster centers.\n\n    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n            dtype=floating\n        The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\n\n    labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\n        The label for each sample. This array is modified in place.\n\n    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples,), dtype=floating\n        The upper bound on the distance between each sample and its closest\n        cluster center. This array is modified in place.\n\n    lower_bounds : ndarray, of shape(n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\n        The lower bound on the distance between each sample and each cluster\n        center. This array is modified in place.\n\n    n_threads : int\n        The number of threads to be used by openmp.\n    \"\"\"\n    cdef:\n        int n_samples = X.shape[0]\n        int n_clusters = centers.shape[0]\n        int n_features = X.shape[1]\n\n        floating min_dist, dist\n        int best_cluster, i, j\n\n    for i in prange(\n        n_samples, num_threads=n_threads, schedule='static', nogil=True\n    ):\n        best_cluster = 0\n        min_dist = _euclidean_dense_dense(&X[i, 0], &centers[0, 0],\n                                          n_features, True)\n        lower_bounds[i, 0] = min_dist\n        for j in range(1, n_clusters):\n            if min_dist > center_half_distances[best_cluster, j]:\n                dist = _euclidean_dense_dense(&X[i, 0], &centers[j, 0],\n                                              n_features, True)\n                lower_bounds[i, j] = dist\n                if dist < min_dist:\n                    min_dist = dist\n                    best_cluster = j\n        labels[i] = best_cluster\n        upper_bounds[i] = min_dist\n\n\ndef init_bounds_sparse(\n        X,                                             #
